      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer205966584872685541">For twelve long years, the dread fortress of Azkaban held an infamous prisoner named Sirius Black. Convicted of killing thirteen people with a single curse, he was said to be the heir apparent to the Dark Lord, Voldemort. <br /><br />Now he has escaped, leaving only two clues as to where he might be headed: Harry Potter's defeat of You-Know-Who was Black's downfall as well; and the Az</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText205966584872685541">For twelve long years, the dread fortress of Azkaban held an infamous prisoner named Sirius Black. Convicted of killing thirteen people with a single curse, he was said to be the heir apparent to the Dark Lord, Voldemort. <br /><br />Now he has escaped, leaving only two clues as to where he might be headed: Harry Potter's defeat of You-Know-Who was Black's downfall as well; and the Azkaban guards heard Black muttering in his sleep, "He's at Hogwarts . . . he's at Hogwarts."<br /><br />Harry Potter isn't safe, not even within the walls of his magical school, surrounded by his friends. Because on top of it all, there may well be a traitor in their midst.</span>

<div class="communityQuestionAndAnswer">
<div class="communityQuestion">
<div class="questionText">
<a href="/questions/326354-when-ron-harry-and-hermoine-were-at">When Ron, harry and hermoine were at hagrid's place during bugbeak's execution, the future selves of harry and hermoine should've also present at that scene. Now since Remus was spectating all this on the Marauder's map, how come did he not observe two sightings of both harry and hermoine on the map?</a>
</div>

<div class="communityAnswerTextContainer">
<span class="communityAnswererName">
<a href="/user/show/21365690-de-wet">De Wet</a>
</span>
<span class="communityAnswerText">
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Time travelling is always tricky to handle. For me it was perhaps the weakest spot in the book, but in an otherwise cracking read like this I'm happy<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Time travelling is always tricky to handle. For me it was perhaps the weakest spot in the book, but in an otherwise cracking read like this I'm happy to just let things go without over analyzing them. Not much point spoiling my enjoyment of a book by trying to do science and logic on fictional magic.<a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8196203832650373836">Lupin was beast</span>

    <br />

    <span class="xhrCommentFooter greyText">
       7 de Ene 08:38
    </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_14146684">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14146684" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/858949-chris" class="left imgcol" title="Chris"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1208350750p2/858949.jpg" alt="Chris" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/14146684?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 09, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/858949-chris" class="user" title="Chris">Chris</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/464164.Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" title="Paperback 9780747546290" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=harry-potter" class="actionLinkLite">harry-potter</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer14146684">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17485026504470038752"><em>Since pretty much everyone I know has read these books, I figure reviewing them is pretty pointless. But with the new book coming out in a couple of weeks, I have to go through them beginning to end. To make the reviews more entertaining, I will be doing them in a variety of unexpected formats. For this review, I will be writing as Crookshanks fan fiction.</em><br /><br />Crookshanks swished his tail back and forth as he crept up the stairs to the boys' bedrooms. He knew the rat wasn't what it was pretending to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17485026504470038752"><em>Since pretty much everyone I know has read these books, I figure reviewing them is pretty pointless. But with the new book coming out in a couple of weeks, I have to go through them beginning to end. To make the reviews more entertaining, I will be doing them in a variety of unexpected formats. For this review, I will be writing as Crookshanks fan fiction.</em><br /><br />Crookshanks swished his tail back and forth as he crept up the stairs to the boys' bedrooms. He knew the rat wasn't what it was pretending to be, but all of his attempts to alert the humans to this fact had failed. "I don't know why I even bother," he muttered to himself. "I could get along fine without any of them. Let the rat do whatever it is it's trying to do. So long as Girl keeps feeding me and scratching my belly, I'll - hello, what's this?"<br /><br />He could smell the rat. Its scent was like nothing Crookshanks had ever smelled, and for all his time living in a magical pet shop, he'd smelled a lot. The rat did smell like a rat, yes, but there was also something else. Something... human. It was just like that big black dog he'd met on the grounds the other day. Every instinct in him had screamed to run away, but there was that smell. And even Crookshanks knew what they said about cats and curiosity. The dog had turned out to be more than just a dog, and it had convinced Crookshanks to help it. First order of business: retrieve a certain rat from the bedroom of the Red-Haired Boy.<br /><br />The Boy wasn't in, but the rat was. Crookshanks circled the bed a few times. This time, maybe, he would be able to get the damn thing. He tensed for a moment and then leapt onto the bed.<br /><br />By luck or skill, he was nearly on top of the thing when he landed. "A-HA!" he yowled. "Gotcha!" He pinned the rat under his sizable paw. "Where you gonna run to now, ratty?" he asked, sneering as best he could.<br /><br />The rat writhed in his grip. "Please," it said. "Just let me go. You don't know what will happen if you eat me, it would be a terrible mistake!"<br /><br />"A mistake, eh?" the cat said. "We'll see about that. I have a great big doggie friend who's just aching to get his jaws around you...."<br /><br />He barely had time to finish his sentence when the rat went mad. It squealed and bit and slashed with its paws. And then, against all of Crookshanks' previous experience - it grew! It nearly threw the cat off the bed as it became much more massive - its legs lengthened and its arms stretched until it had reached a human size and shape. Crookshanks goggled. Of all the things he'd expected from this rat, this wasn't it. The human grabbed at him, but Crookshanks was too fast. He jumped off the bed and shimmied under the wardrobe, where he could see but not be seen.<br /><br />The human looked around, breathing heavily. He was pale and thin, and still looked ratty. "Think, Peter, think," he said. "Gotta get out of here, but..." He stopped, glanced at the wardrobe, and grimaced. "You may just have given me my way out, cat," he said. And then he bit the ball of his hand.<br /><br />Blood dripped out, leaving spreading red blotches on the sheets. "They'll think it was you," he said. "They'll leave me for dead and I'll be free to rejoin my Lord." He looked at the recently repaired curtains on Ron's bed. "It's not safe here anymore." He sucked at the wound to stop the bloodflow and then went to the window. Perched on the windowsill, he looked over at Crookshanks' hiding place. "If I were human," he said, "the fall would kill me. But as a rat...." His body rippled and twisted and shrank, and then there was an old grey rat on the sill. Crookshanks was pretty sure it winked at him before leaping off.<br /><br />After a minute or two, Crookshanks wriggled out from under the wardrobe, his thoughts dark. The Red-Haired Boy was going to be angry, and so was the Girl. But more importantly, the Dog was going to be furious. It was barely holding on to its sanity as it was. Crookshanks shook his head. This was going to get worse before it would get better...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17485026504470038752">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/108852877?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 02, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3452652-raeleen-lemay" class="user" title="Raeleen Lemay">Raeleen Lemay</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/464164.Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" title="Paperback 9780747546290" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3452652-raeleen-lemay?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3452652-raeleen-lemay?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer108852877">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3823259698931823414"><em>Re-Read in December 2014 for Harry Christmas to You</em><br /><br />OH MAN. THIS BOOK IS SO MY FAVORITE.<br /><br />The phone conversation at the beginning between Ron and Uncle Vernon was PRICELESS. I wish so much that that scene had been in the movie.<br /><br />I was so into reading this book that I failed to take notes, so I don't have many specifics to add except that I love how Crookshanks was basically Sirius's secret agent spy cat friend and I LOVE THAT.<br /><br />Also, this book demonstrated some very REAL aspects of school. For example,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3823259698931823414"><em>Re-Read in December 2014 for Harry Christmas to You</em><br /><br />OH MAN. THIS BOOK IS SO MY FAVORITE.<br /><br />The phone conversation at the beginning between Ron and Uncle Vernon was PRICELESS. I wish so much that that scene had been in the movie.<br /><br />I was so into reading this book that I failed to take notes, so I don't have many specifics to add except that I love how Crookshanks was basically Sirius's secret agent spy cat friend and I LOVE THAT.<br /><br />Also, this book demonstrated some very REAL aspects of school. For example, Hermione took on too much work, and she gradually started to go crazy (and consequently distanced herself from her friends, became more moody, and then finally just bitch-slapped Malfoy). I also found Oliver Wood to be hilarious in this book for similar reasons: this was his last year at Hogwarts, and he wanted nothing more than to win the Quidditch Cup so he could have some sort of glory at Hogwarts, and he became so consumed by it (as I'm sure lots of people on sports teams do). The way he was so emotionally invested really cracked me up but also felt so real. <br /><br />Side note: CEDRIC IS SO DAMN NICE. when he realized that Harry fell off his broom during the Quidditch game and Hufflepuff won he called for a rematch, which says a lot about him, and it just makes what happens in the next book that much worse.<br /><br />But of course, all of the Marauders stuff made my inner fangirl go nuts because it has to be my favorite Harry Potter storyline. (I mean, I didn't name my YouTube channel after them or anything...)<br /><br />Also time travel.</span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer154780344">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2736457920481958685">Literally one of the best books I've ever read. I was chained to it for two days. I cried and laughed and yelled SHIT when all of the action went down.<br /><br />I'm such a peasant for judging this series before I had read it. I read the first two and half of this one when I was about 10, before reading was cool, before I had the attention span that reading requires (I know these are kids' books but I was a particularly distracted child). I did not know, Mother Rowling. Forgive my sin, and all the times wh</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2736457920481958685">Literally one of the best books I've ever read. I was chained to it for two days. I cried and laughed and yelled SHIT when all of the action went down.<br /><br />I'm such a peasant for judging this series before I had read it. I read the first two and half of this one when I was about 10, before reading was cool, before I had the attention span that reading requires (I know these are kids' books but I was a particularly distracted child). I did not know, Mother Rowling. Forgive my sin, and all the times when I said, "I don't think Harry Potter is really my thing". Please.<br /><br />This book was incredible and this series is a classic more than any Dickens or Middle Earth or Narnia shit has any right to be. This series isn't up it's own ass; it's so accessible and readable and meaningful.<br /><br />God damn me! How could I have been so blind?<br /><br />Forgive me, because this book changed the game. This book deserves 7 stars and I'm getting the cover art (from my edition) tattooed on my thigh.<br /><br />I'm such a fucking <em>fan</em>.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1465110878">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1465110878" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6168268-delee" class="left imgcol" title="Delee"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1431034088p2/6168268.jpg" alt="Delee" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1465110878?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 04, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6168268-delee" class="user" title="Delee">Delee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5.Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780439655484" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6168268-delee?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6168268-delee?shelf=ya" class="actionLinkLite">ya</a>,

              <a href="/review/list/6168268-delee?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>,

              <a href="/review/list/6168268-delee?shelf=stepheny-made-me" class="actionLinkLite">stepheny-made-me</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1465110878">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10693523443694674446">Buddy-read with two of my Great Escape gal pals- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241902728?comment=145377249#comment_145377249">Stepheny</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104910588">Ivonne</a>.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo 8c2dfbee-747b-4477-853c-86940b726771_zpsfet1adlx.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451887137i/17616722.jpg" /><br /><br />Be on the look out for Stepheny Potthead aka The Book Pusher aka Quick Draw Stepheny aka The Nutty Professor. Last seen running along side the Knight Bus with Harry Potter's invisible cloak. Also Suspected in the kidnapping of fellow Goodreader Jeff and best-selling author Stephen King. Blonde Hair...big green doll eyes, has a frightening maniacal cackle and a tendency to whine when she doesn't get her way. LOUDLY. Considered a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10693523443694674446">Buddy-read with two of my Great Escape gal pals- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241902728?comment=145377249#comment_145377249">Stepheny</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104910588">Ivonne</a>.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo 8c2dfbee-747b-4477-853c-86940b726771_zpsfet1adlx.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451887137i/17616722.jpg" /><br /><br />Be on the look out for Stepheny Potthead aka The Book Pusher aka Quick Draw Stepheny aka The Nutty Professor. Last seen running along side the Knight Bus with Harry Potter's invisible cloak. Also Suspected in the kidnapping of fellow Goodreader Jeff and best-selling author Stephen King. Blonde Hair...big green doll eyes, has a frightening maniacal cackle and a tendency to whine when she doesn't get her way. LOUDLY. Considered armed and dangerous- approach with caution...and Nerds- she likes Nerds.<br /><br />Now back to our regularly scheduled review....<br /><br />I don't listen to a lot of audio-books (I prefer to read) but I was kind of falling behind in my reading commitments...and I had put Ms. Stepheny off again and again for this buddy-read soooooo many times- I couldn't do it again to her (she pouts..and she gets all mopey and it is JUST heartbreaking). I am so happy I listened to this one- Stephen Fry was just perfect. Perfect!..and HARRY POTTER AND THE PRISONER OF AZKABAN was just the thing to put me in the Christmas Spirit. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo d51ae6fc-03d0-4b40-b874-97ea5a32aa63_zps6vo1u0fq.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451887137i/17616723.jpg" /><br /><br />It's Harry's least favorite time of year- school break spent with the Dursleys...and this visit isn't going well. First: News that Sirius Black has escaped from Azkaban- Second: An unfortunate accident involving mean Aunt Marge...<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo a7ff8064-9033-464d-b889-658eceb341fe_zpsatrxuapa.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451887137i/17616724.jpg" /><br /><br />Harry decides not to stick around- and catches the Knight Bus to Diagon Alley- where instead of getting in trouble for using magic away from Hogwarts, he gets invited to stay until school begins, by Cornelius Fudge-the Minister for Magic.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo c7e24bac-45b7-432e-8533-fe006f247450_zpscu29pvjp.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451887137i/17616725.jpg" /><br /><br />The night before he is expected to leave- Harry is warned that Sirius may have escaped with murder in mind- and HE may be the target....<br /><br />This is my favorite of the series so far!! I loved that it was still light and fun...but that the darkness is slooooooooowly creeping in.<br /><br />I loved that a lot of it took place during the Christmas Holidays...<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo bb1d20ee-dd9d-4eab-9fe8-c2722a4e0e75_zpskjbirexq.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451887138i/17616727.jpg" /><br /><br />I really liked the addition of the Dementors...spoooooky...<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo 757e5100-3fef-4bf7-87bc-0cf6c603852b_zpsl9sagtcu.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451887137i/17616726.jpg" /><br /><br />...and I adored Buckbeak!!<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo ff169a79-0f81-4477-94f4-bd6f5b23efba_zpsz5vic02h.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451887138i/17616728.jpg" /><br /><br />As for the whereabouts of Stepheny? I can almost guarantee...she is up to no good.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo 21fac931-9a35-4f5c-8369-e0a3b87a5d8a_zps2h4uwd2c.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451887138i/17616729.jpg" /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10693523443694674446">...more</a>

  <a href="/user/show/1022982-brad" class="left imgcol" title="Brad"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" alt="Brad" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/18611960?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 02, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1022982-brad" class="user" title="Brad">Brad</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/464164.Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" title="Paperback 9780747546290" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=faves" class="actionLinkLite">faves</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=youth" class="actionLinkLite">youth</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=to-my-kids" class="actionLinkLite">to-my-kids</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=out-loud" class="actionLinkLite">out-loud</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer18611960">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13763843672708444206">I know that many of you out there haven't gotten around to reading <a title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (Harry Potter, #3) by J.K. Rowling" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5.Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban__Harry_Potter___3_">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a>. Much like Umberto Eco's <a title="Foucault's Pendulum by Umberto Eco" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17841.Foucault_s_Pendulum">Foucault's Pendulum</a>, Germaine Greer's <a title="The Female Eunuch by Germaine Greer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/98532.The_Female_Eunuch">The Female Eunuch</a> and Lucifer's worldwide bestseller <a title="Holy Bible The New King James Version by Anonymous" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2284803.Holy_Bible_The_New_King_James_Version">The Holy Bible</a>, you own a copy, it gathers dust, but its never been read. You've been thinking about it, though. You see it there on the shelf and you wonder, "Is this book for me?"<br /><br />The following checklist will tell you all you need to know about <a title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (Harry Potter, #3) by J.K. Rowling" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5.Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban__Harry_Potter___3_">Harry Potter and the Prisoner</a></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13763843672708444206">I know that many of you out there haven't gotten around to reading <a title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (Harry Potter, #3) by J.K. Rowling" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5.Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban__Harry_Potter___3_">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a>. Much like Umberto Eco's <a title="Foucault's Pendulum by Umberto Eco" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17841.Foucault_s_Pendulum">Foucault's Pendulum</a>, Germaine Greer's <a title="The Female Eunuch by Germaine Greer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/98532.The_Female_Eunuch">The Female Eunuch</a> and Lucifer's worldwide bestseller <a title="Holy Bible The New King James Version by Anonymous" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2284803.Holy_Bible_The_New_King_James_Version">The Holy Bible</a>, you own a copy, it gathers dust, but its never been read. You've been thinking about it, though. You see it there on the shelf and you wonder, "Is this book for me?"<br /><br />The following checklist will tell you all you need to know about <a title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (Harry Potter, #3) by J.K. Rowling" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5.Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban__Harry_Potter___3_">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a>'s suitability for you. The more checkmarks you have, the more you need to tackle this wonder of modern literature.<br /><br />1. Do you have Daddy issues? ? or ?<br />2. Has a creepy middle aged man been sleeping with you for years, unbeknownst to you? ? or ?<br />3. Does the full moon make you anxious? ? or ?<br />4. Have you ever gorged on chocolate to combat depression? ? or ?<br />5. Do you find there just isn't enough time in the day? ? or ?<br />6. Are you misunderstood? ? or ?<br />7. Do you have an overactive sense of justice that gets you into trouble? ? or ?<br />8. Do you break rules whenever you can? ? or ?<br />9. Do you scoff at personal danger, especially when it gets in the way of your fun? ? or ?<br />10. Are you a dog lover, or would you like to be one? ? or ?<br /><br /><br />1-2: You'd probably rather be reading <a title="Finnegans Wake (Penguin Twentieth-Century Classics) by James Joyce" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/442140.Finnegans_Wake__Penguin_Twentieth_Century_Classics_">Finnegan's Wake</a>, <a title="The Book of Mormon Another Testament of Jesus Christ (Official Edition) by The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/323355.The_Book_of_Mormon_Another_Testament_of_Jesus_Christ__Official_Edition_">The Book of Mormon</a> or <a title="Dick And Jane Fun Wherever We Are by Anonymous" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/938600.Dick_And_Jane_Fun_Wherever_We_Are">Sally Dick and Jane</a><br />3-5: Skip it and watch the movie.<br />6-8: Time to dust off that copy and give it a whirl.<br />9-10: Put your existential crisis aside. Shave your moustache. Take a day off work, and read this book. It won't change your life, but it'll be like reading about your dream self.<br /><br />Do as you will. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13763843672708444206">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_119044">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119044" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7577-pinkgal" class="left imgcol" title="pinkgal"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1232473322p2/7577.jpg" alt="pinkgal" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/119044?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 17, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7577-pinkgal" class="user" title="pinkgal">pinkgal</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/4256.Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" title="Hardcover 9780747573623" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7577-pinkgal?shelf=absolute-favorites" class="actionLinkLite">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7577-pinkgal?shelf=magic_fairytale-esque" class="actionLinkLite">magic_fairytale-esque</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer119044">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12979302558884346851">It was September 1998; the third Harry Potter book had just been released. Pottermania? What's that? It was still unknown except to a vast population of younglings who'd read it... and I fell in love. Oh, how I fell in love. I fell in love with the poor, starved-for-affection, later known to be a twit Harry. I fell in love with the pretentious know-it-all Hermione. I fell in love with the awkward, grew-up-in-his-brother's-shadows Ron... and most of all? I fell in love with the snarky, unplatable</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12979302558884346851">It was September 1998; the third Harry Potter book had just been released. Pottermania? What's that? It was still unknown except to a vast population of younglings who'd read it... and I fell in love. Oh, how I fell in love. I fell in love with the poor, starved-for-affection, later known to be a twit Harry. I fell in love with the pretentious know-it-all Hermione. I fell in love with the awkward, grew-up-in-his-brother's-shadows Ron... and most of all? I fell in love with the snarky, unplatable, snarling, rude, hygienically-disinclined professor of potions, Severus Snape. <br /><br />Almost ten years later, I'm still obsessed with it in many ways. <br /><br />I think this is my favorite of all the Harry Potter books thus far. This is the one that introduces Sirius Black, who I sometimes loathe (only sometimes!) and Remus Lupin, who I will always, always love. And of course, this is the book that gave us one piece of Severus Snape's background. And that was the infamous Prank that may or may not have destroyed Snape's trust in Dumbledore. Would you have trusted someone who didn't at least suspend the one who'd tried to kill you? I don't think so. This is also the book where I found myself looking at Dumbledore with a new eye. He's a crafty old fella, I tell you that. He'll do anything to gain his means, regardless of how he may personally feel on the matter. Grandpa Albus, he ain't. <br /><br />And Severus Snape, my heart did bleed for thee. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12979302558884346851">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_542175849">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/542175849?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 02, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously" class="user" title="Rachel ?Reads Ravenously? ">Rachel ?Reads Ravenously? </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer542175849">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7885059570915589978"><strong> 5 Expecto Patronum stars! </strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434732912ra/15257141.gif" /><br /><br />I grew up with Harry Potter. Yes, I am that generation. I was a little bit younger than 11 when the books were released, and when the final book was published I had just graduated high school. I'm also the same age as Daniel Radcliffe and he's only older than me by less than a month. I also have a deathly hallows bumper sticker on my car. So, I think it's safe to say that this series has had a profound effect on me, to the point where I am still a little bit bitter tha</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7885059570915589978"><strong> 5 Expecto Patronum stars! </strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434732912ra/15257141.gif" /><br /><br />I grew up with Harry Potter. Yes, I am that generation. I was a little bit younger than 11 when the books were released, and when the final book was published I had just graduated high school. I'm also the same age as Daniel Radcliffe and he's only older than me by less than a month. I also have a deathly hallows bumper sticker on my car. So, I think it's safe to say that this series has had a profound effect on me, to the point where I am still a little bit bitter that I never got my Hogwarts acceptance letter.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434732912ra/15257142.gif" /><br /><br />A couple years ago I reread the first two books in the series and loved them just as much as when I was a kid. So when I got into a horrible reading slump, I saw my dad watching Harry Potter weekend on ABC Family (as he does for every fucking Harry Potter weekend mind you), I said to myself, what the hell. Time for a reread. So hence, Harry Potter 3 reread. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434732912ra/15257143.gif" /><br /><br />All of us may know the story but I am going to reiterate. In his third year at Hogwarts, Harry Potter learns that a dangerous man named Sirius Black has escaped from the wizard prison Azkaban. Harry then overhears the fact that Black is the reason his parents are dead, as Black sold them out to Voldemort and then killed 13 people in broad daylight. <br /><br /><strong> So in a unique part of the review from me, here are all the amazing parts of this book that I forgot because I've been watching the movies instead: </strong><br /><br /><strong>-Peeves the Poltergeist:</strong> Holy crap how did I forget about this hilarious menacing spirit? He's not as present in this book but he has always had a part in the series and I completely forgot he existed! I know they can't include everything in the movies but I wish Peeves had been included.<br /><br /><strong>-Charlie Weasley:</strong> Ron had yet ANOTHER sibling that is only mentioned in the films! This one is the cool brother in Egypt.<br /><br /><strong>-Cho Chang and Cedric Diggory:</strong> there are soooooo many mentions of Cho and Cedric in this book! I never really noticed Cedric until the 4th book where he becomes prominent. And this is the book where Harry's crush on Cho began. Stomach flutters!<br /><br /><strong>-More details on Whomping Willow/Shrieking Shack:</strong> This may be a spoiler for those of you who haven't read it, but the Whomping Willow was actually planted to hide Lupin's werewolfism as well as the shrieking shack to hide him. I thought this little tidbit was super interesting, along with the details of how Black escaped Azkaban. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434732912ra/15257144.gif" /><br /><br />And just in general, I love JK Rowling's ability to tie things together. There's so much in this book that becomes important later and tiny little details and sharp wit that make me giggle. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434732912ra/15257145.gif" /><br /><br />So in a small factoid, this book is probably my least favorite of the entire series. It's good, obviously, but for some reason I like all the other ones better. The movie, well it's my second to last favorite (just ahead of that godawful Goblet of Fire film which ruined everything but I digress). The movie director added so many unnecessary things that weren't in the book, and I wish he hadn't so he could of kept the good stuff! (And I've heard a rumor that he didn't even read the fucking book until JK kept vetoing all of his weird ideas. Look it up!)<br /><br />If you haven't read these books, do not tell me!!!!! I will smack you!<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434732912ra/15257146.gif" /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7885059570915589978">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1269178454">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10620271212913023604">Reread November 2015<br /><br />It took me over a month to read this, because I have been so busy with college. It definitely got in the way of my reading experience, but I loved POA nonetheless! It has been two or three years since I've read it and I forgot so much! <br /><br />My only complaint is that there were a lot of references to events in previous books. She explained Quidditch again, told us who Ron and Hermione are, what happened at the end of last school year... And to me, that wasn't necessary.<br /><br />There are so</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10620271212913023604">Reread November 2015<br /><br />It took me over a month to read this, because I have been so busy with college. It definitely got in the way of my reading experience, but I loved POA nonetheless! It has been two or three years since I've read it and I forgot so much! <br /><br />My only complaint is that there were a lot of references to events in previous books. She explained Quidditch again, told us who Ron and Hermione are, what happened at the end of last school year... And to me, that wasn't necessary.<br /><br />There are some differences between the film and book (not as many as the later books/films though), but I don't really mind! The film is my absolute favourite, I like the changes they've made (expect for leaving out information about the Marauders) so I don't really know which one I actually prefer :) <br /><br />JK Rowling really needs to come out with a prequel ASAP! I love this book so much because of the Marauders, and I wish we knew more about them and their era. I think we can all agree that we'd prefer a prequel over a sequel, such as The Cursed Child. And yes, I know about Fantastic Beasts, but that's not really Potter related so that doesn't count ;) </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer794900318">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7161643573067155552"><strong> <blockquote>“I solemnly swear that I am up to no good.”</blockquote> </strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421858468i/13422530._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Wasn't this epic. Didn't this stun you into silence after reading it.<br /><br />These are rhetorical. So, don't bother answering because I already know what you'll say. You'll agree with me that this is by far the best Harry Potter novel, and I'll add that I just couldn't put it down, nor did I want to.<br /><br />This was great, this was stunning, this was grand. I loved it so much. This was a tad bit scary too, considering the previous two novels. I think Harry is growing</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7161643573067155552"><strong>
  <blockquote>“I solemnly swear that I am up to no good.”</blockquote>
</strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421858468i/13422530._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Wasn't this epic. Didn't this stun you into silence after reading it.<br /><br />These are rhetorical. So, don't bother answering because I already know what you'll say. You'll agree with me that this is by far the best Harry Potter novel, and I'll add that I just couldn't put it down, nor did I want to.<br /><br />This was great, this was stunning, this was grand. I loved it so much. This was a tad bit scary too, considering the previous two novels. I think Harry is growing up, so do Ron &amp; Hermione. Our little heroes are no longer babies, they are growing up fast and I am gladly keeping up with them.<br /><br />Is there any other way to say that I loved what J. K. Rowling did with Wormtail, I loved how it was all a big twist. I loved how things were so unpredictable and you didn't know what to get ready for next.<br /><br />This was thrilling and exhilarating. I was just reading and reading and reading like a junkie addicted to their drug, that was my brand of heroine for sure..<br /><br />I loved Sirius and I loved Remus. I loved everything about this. I love the relationship between Harry, Ron &amp; Hermione. They all fit together, they need no one else. It's just them three and it's enough because they know that they'll always have together, and no matter what they'll stick together because that's what friends are for. And being different people, having diffent personalities doesn't bring us apart, it brings people together. It makes the friendship more interesting, more unpredictable. <br /><br /><strong>
  <blockquote>“Mischief managed.”</blockquote>
</strong></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1117944488?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 29, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell" class="user" title="Maxwell">Maxwell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17347383-harry-potter-and-the-prisoner-of-azkaban" title="Paperback 9780545582933" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=i-own-it" class="actionLinkLite">i-own-it</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=2014" class="actionLinkLite">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1117944488">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10503186393431224366"><em>Reread November 2014</em><br /><br />The third film is my favorite of the series because it's a bit darker than the previous too, and the story gets creepier and moodier with the unfolding of Sirius Black's tale. However, I don't think the third book is my favorite to read. I do <em>love</em> the whole Time-Turner/Inception situation that goes on near the end. And the introduction of Lupin and Black are such great additions to the series (and Buckbeak, but what ever happens to him?). <br /><br />I'm really enjoying these rereads, an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10503186393431224366"><em>Reread November 2014</em><br /><br />The third film is my favorite of the series because it's a bit darker than the previous too, and the story gets creepier and moodier with the unfolding of Sirius Black's tale. However, I don't think the third book is my favorite to read. I do <em>love</em> the whole Time-Turner/Inception situation that goes on near the end. And the introduction of Lupin and Black are such great additions to the series (and Buckbeak, but what ever happens to him?). <br /><br />I'm really enjoying these rereads, and it makes me even more excited to get into books 4-7 because I haven't reread those books in so long! And the kids get older, the story gets more intense, and everything begins to unravel and you have to try and start putting the pieces back together. <br /><br />Here, as I've done with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1116433719?book_show_action=false">Sorcerer's Stone</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1116981984?book_show_action=false">Chamber of Secrets</a>, are some of my thoughts from rereading the 3rd book:<br />-Hermione's boggart is McGonagall telling her she's failed all her subjects haha.<br />-For not liking Scabbers as a pet that much, Ron really has a hard time letting him go when Sirius asks to prove he is Pettigrew<br />-"Ron put his weight gingerly on the leg"- ok Rowling, a ginger pun? Great.<br />-At one point when they're healing in the hopsital wing, Hermione is described as looking 'petrified.' #TBT<br />-Also, Madame Pomfrey's first name is Poppy. Poppy Pomfrey. What.<br /><br />Again, 5/5 stars because SIRIUS BLACK AND ALL THE FEELS.<br /></span>

          </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7924099404454898842">This honestly has to have one of best plots in the Harry Potter series! It's so well devised and was perfectly planned out from the very start, utterly fantastic!!<br /><br />Prisoner of Azkaban will always be one of my favourites in the series, both book and film, because I feel like we really get to learn a lot about the characters and the wizarding world.<br /><br />I love getting to know more about the marauders and I nEED to know more! It honestly breaks my heart when reading this because Lupin and Sirius really did deserve so much better!<br /><br />So glad I reread this! <div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_241902728">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241902728" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny" class="left imgcol" title="Stepheny"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446648446p2/7091879.jpg" alt="Stepheny" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/241902728?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 04, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny" class="user" title="Stepheny">Stepheny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13611643-harry-potter-and-the-prisoner-of-azkaban" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=books-everyone-should-read" class="actionLinkLite">books-everyone-should-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=favorite-series" class="actionLinkLite">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=ya" class="actionLinkLite">ya</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=coming-of-age" class="actionLinkLite">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=like-a-meth-addiction" class="actionLinkLite">like-a-meth-addiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=badd-ass-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">badd-ass-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=guilty-pleasure-reads" class="actionLinkLite">guilty-pleasure-reads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=reliving-my-childhood" class="actionLinkLite">reliving-my-childhood</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer241902728">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15316748085273490771"><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241902710?book_show_action=false">My own journey</a> with Harry Potter started a long time ago. But when Delee mentioned she had never read it before I knew I had to change that. And I think some deeper part of her understood that if our friendship were to stand the test of time she would have to read them. When she <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900860104?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1"> gave 5 stars to book 1</a> I knew I had her! <br /><br />And sure enough we made our way to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241902773">Chamber of Secrets</a>.I was unsure what she would make of the second book. It seems to be the most criticized. Many state that it is too much like</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15316748085273490771"><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241902710?book_show_action=false">My own journey</a> with Harry Potter started a long time ago. But when Delee mentioned she had never read it before I knew I had to change that. And I think some deeper part of her understood that if our friendship were to stand the test of time she would have to read them. When she <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900860104?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1"> gave 5 stars to book 1</a> I knew I had her! <br /><br />And sure enough we made our way to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241902773">Chamber of Secrets</a>.I was unsure what she would make of the second book. It seems to be the most criticized. Many state that it is too much like the first one and that it doesn't serve much purpose. I tend to give people a heads up that the first 3 books of the series in general are aimed at a much younger crowd than the last 4. I have to say I was shocked but very excited to see that once again, Delee had given <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1268939794?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1"> 5 shiny stars</a> to Chamber as well. <br /><br />So here we are. Our journey began in March of 2014 and I have been trying my best to be a patient and understanding leader. Sometimes I take her hand and gently guide her, other times I chase her with a wooden spoon threatening severe punishments if she doesn't commit to a date to begin the next book. But I do try to be patient. I hope she knows that. ;) We picked up another buddy for this read- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104910588"> The Enchanting Ivonne</a>. <br /><br />When it comes to the world of Harry Potter there is little that I am unfamiliar with. And there is even less that I won’t do to get people to read it. Now that Delee <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1465110878?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">has the third book under her belt</a> I think it will take less and less persuasion to get her on board for the next one. In fact, we finished this one in December and we’re starting Goblet in March! MARCH. That’s not that far away! <br /><br />Prisoner has been a fan favorite since it came out. I think it was one of the most popular of the movies as well. But it has never been <em>my</em> favorite. Obviously I still love it and it’s a wonderful book, but in the grand scheme of things it falls lower on my list than most other Pottheads’. <br /><br />A crazy murdering psycho is on the loose. His name is Sirius Black and he has somehow escaped the Wizard prison- Azkaban. No one, and I do mean no one, has ever done this before. Now, this isn't some wimpy old Muggle prison like Alcatraz.We are talking the big time here folks. The place is packed with dementors! They suck the happiness and life right out of you. They make you so incredibly sad and sorrowful that you’ll be left with no hope.<br /><br />So how did Black do it? How was he able to remain sane in a place as awful as Azkaban? They say he was lucid and even downright chatty whenever the Minister for Magic had to do a check on the prison. Is he just that crazy that the dementors don’t affect him? Most importantly- <strong>why</strong> did he escape? <br /><br />But Harry soon finds out that Black has come to finish what he started 12 years earlier. He has come to kill Harry.<br /><br />Prisoner offers a break in what was perceived as the “formula”. In this one we learn to battle our depression. We learn to find our happiest moments in our weakest and most awful ones. We learn to forgive and we learn to show mercy. We learn what it means to have a second chance. And we are introduced to Buckbeak. <br /><br />Prisoner of Azkaban is a great story and added a nice dynamic to the Harry Potter series. It is the only one like it within the series where the other ones can be compared fairly easily to one another. <br /><br />I am so thankful to have such an incredible friend agree to accompany me on this journey. I am so thankful that she trusts me to guide her. But mostly I am so thankful that we can share these stories together. It is a bonding experience like no other. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15316748085273490771">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KJV3W2bfvNQ+jgsYScGO0ipUAMKmMRlpZUzzC7Tbdi9NQUiIlA2oLrJWf6M3oGhgY6PD2+/sXsMPRfaZeE6Aag==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling">About J.K. Rowling</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling"><img alt="1077326" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1415945171p2/1077326.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer6107315639279235837">See also: <a title="Robert Galbraith" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/383606.Robert_Galbraith">Robert Galbraith</a><br />Although she writes under the pen name <strong>J.K. Rowling</strong>, pronounced like <em>rolling</em>, her name when her first <em>Harry Potter</em> book was published was simply <strong>Joanne Rowling</strong>. Anticipating that the target audience of young boys might not want to read a book written by a woman, her publishers demanded that she use two initials, rather than her full name. As she had no middle name, she ch</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6107315639279235837">See also: <a title="Robert Galbraith" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/383606.Robert_Galbraith">Robert Galbraith</a><br />Although she writes under the pen name <strong>J.K. Rowling</strong>, pronounced like <em>rolling</em>, her name when her first <em>Harry Potter</em> book was published was simply <strong>Joanne Rowling</strong>. Anticipating that the target audience of young boys might not want to read a book written by a woman, her publishers demanded that she use two initials, rather than her full name. As she had no middle name, she chose <strong>K</strong> as the second initial of her pen name, from her paternal grandmother Kathleen Ada Bulgen Rowling. She calls herself <strong>Jo</strong> and has said, "No one ever called me 'Joanne' when I was young, unless they were angry." Following her marriage, she has sometimes used the name <strong>Joanne Murray</strong> when conducting personal business. During the Leveson Inquiry she gave evidence under the name of <strong>Joanne Kathleen Rowling</strong>. In a 2012 interview, Rowling noted that she no longer cared that people pronounced her name incorrectly.<br /><br />Rowling was born to Peter James Rowling, a Rolls-Royce aircraft engineer, and Anne Rowling (née Volant), on 31 July 1965 in Yate, Gloucestershire, England, 10 miles (16 km) northeast of Bristol. Her mother Anne was half-French and half-Scottish. Her parents first met on a train departing from King's Cross Station bound for Arbroath in 1964. They married on 14 March 1965. Her mother's maternal grandfather, Dugald Campbell, was born in Lamlash on the Isle of Arran. Her mother's paternal grandfather, Louis Volant, was awarded the Croix de Guerre for exceptional bravery in defending the village of Courcelles-le-Comte during the First World War.<br /><br />Rowling's sister Dianne was born at their home when Rowling was 23 months old. The family moved to the nearby village Winterbourne when Rowling was four. She attended St Michael's Primary School, a school founded by abolitionist William Wilberforce and education reformer Hannah More. Her headmaster at St Michael's, Alfred Dunn, has been suggested as the inspiration for the <em>Harry Potter</em> headmaster Albus Dumbledore.<br /><br />As a child, Rowling often wrote fantasy stories, which she would usually then read to her sister. She recalls that: "I can still remember me telling her a story in which she fell down a rabbit hole and was fed strawberries by the rabbit family inside it. Certainly the first story I ever wrote down (when I was five or six) was about a rabbit called Rabbit. He got the measles and was visited by his friends, including a giant bee called Miss Bee." At the age of nine, Rowling moved to Church Cottage in the Gloucestershire village of Tutshill, close to Chepstow, Wales. When she was a young teenager, her great aunt, who Rowling said "taught classics and approved of a thirst for knowledge, even of a questionable kind," gave her a very old copy of Jessica Mitford's autobiography, <em>Hons and Rebels</em>. Mitford became Rowling's heroine, and Rowling subsequently read all of her books.<br /><br />Rowling has said of her teenage years, in an interview with The New Yorker, "I wasn’t particularly happy. I think it’s a dreadful time of life." She had a difficult homelife; her mother was ill and she had a difficult relationship with her father (she is no longer on speaking terms with him). She attended secondary school at Wyedean School and College, where her mother had worked as a technician in the science department. Rowling said of her adolescence, "Hermione [a bookish, know-it-all <em>Harry Potter</em> character] is loosely based on me. She's a caricature of me when I was eleven, which I'm not particularly proud of." Steve Eddy, who taught Rowling English when she first arrived, remembers her as "not exceptional" but "one of a group of girls who were bright, and quite good at English." Sean Harris, her best friend in the Upper Sixth owned a turquoise Ford Anglia, which she says inspired the one in her books.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6107315639279235837">...more</a>

    </div>
